PK31776: ALTER QMGR MAXCHL() REQUIRES CHINIT RESTART IF THE VALUE FOR MAXCHL IS GREATER THAN THAT WHICH THE CHINIT WAS STARTED WITH

Be the first to ask a question 
APAR status

    Closed as documentation error.

Error description

    MAXCHL changes will only be honoured in a running CHINIT
    (copied to the XGWA) IF the new value is <= the value at CHINIT
    initialization.
    .
    If the new value is > the value at CHINIT initialization it will
    remain in the qmgr object and take effect at the next CHINIT
    restart.
    .
    Channels were rejected at the old MAXCHL value, for example
      CSQX513E CSQXRESP Channel CLIENT1 exceeded current channel
      limit
    even though DISPLAY DQM shows the new value in message CSQX840I
    before the recycle.

Local fix

Problem summary

    ****************************************************************
    * USERS AFFECTED: All users of Websphere MQ for z/OS Version 6 *
    ****************************************************************
    * PROBLEM DESCRIPTION: Dynamic changes to the CHINIT values    *
    *                      of ACTCHL and/or MAXCHL made via the    *
    *                      ALTER QMGR command which increase the   *
    *                      values ABOVE those defined at CHINIT    *
    *                      startup REQUIRE a RESTART of the        *
    *                      CHINIT to implement the new values      *
    *                      properly.                               *
    *                      The MQ Script(MQSC) Command Reference   *
    *                      manual SC34-6597-00 does not state      *
    *                      this requirement.                       *
    ****************************************************************
    * RECOMMENDATION:                                              *
    ****************************************************************
    The MAXCHL parameter determines the allocated size of some
    CHINIT tables at CHINIT initialization time, which cannot be
    extended while the CHINIT is running.
    In the BASE V6 code release an attempt to continue running with
    new increased values BEYOND the initial value can cause CHINIT
    Abends - Apar PK29704 prevents this happening by ensuring that
    any LARGER value is not used until the next CHINIT restart.
    This Apar documents this restriction.

Problem conclusion

    The Websphere MQ Script(MQSC) Command Reference manual
    chapter 2. The MQSC commands  in the ALTER QMGR section
    Queue manager parameter decriptions will be updated to
    add the following Notes :
    .
    Under the ACTCHL parameter :-
    ACTCHL changes will only be honoured in a running CHINIT
    IF the new value is <= the value at CHINIT Initialization.
    If the new value is > the value at CHINIT initialization
    it will remain in the qmgr object and take effect at the
    next CHINIT restart.
    .
    Under the MAXCHL parameter :-
    MAXCHL changes will only be honoured in a running CHINIT
    IF the new value is <= the value at CHINIT Initialization.
    If the new value is > the value at CHINIT initialization
    it will remain in the qmgr object and take effect at the
    next CHINIT restart.




http://www-01.ibm.com/support/docview.wss?uid=swg27045669&aid=1

 To aid your understanding of what you are seeng, you must first understand the difference between a channel definition and a running channel instance. Withe SVRCONN channels (also other other type of receiving channels) one channel definition can actually end up being manifested into many running instances, i.e. many different sockets.

If you use the DISPLAY CHANNEL(MYCHANNEL) command you will see one result.

If you use the DISPLAY CHSTATUS(MYCHANNEL) command you will see several results. Each one of these results is a different socket, and each one of these will have a different PID. This is what is controlled by MaxChannels.

Then with the SHARECNV setting with a value of more than 1 (it is 10 by default) you can have multiple client application connections being shared over each socket. This is why you see even more results with your DISPLAY CONN command. You can control how much sharing happens with the SHARECNV attribute on DEFINE CHANNEL.

Sharing can only occur when the connections are coming from the same process on the client side machine, so most likely in an application hosting environment. 

App connections can be client (over a SVRCONN channel, limited by MAX CHANNEL/ACTIVE CHANNEL) or server binding (not limited). DIS CONN shows both types, so there could be 1000's active connection and none of them using client. 



The error AMQ9513 (Maximum number of channels reached. ) is reported in the MQ queue manager error logs when a client application attempts to connect to the queue manager and the specified maximum number of channels are in use.

Procedure

    Copy the JCL to a JES procedure library, for example:

    cp -S d=.jcl ++HBRINSTPATH++/zexecutionserver/wlp/templates/zos/procs/bbgzangl.jcl. "//'SYS1.PROCLIB'"
    copy to clipboard

    Edit the JCL and change the ROOT variable to the value ++HBRINSTPATH++/zexecutionserver/wlp, for example:

    SET ROOT='/usr/lpp/zDM/V8R8M1/zexecutionserver/wlp'

https://www.ibm.com/support/knowledgecenter/en/SSYKE2_6.0.0/com.ibm.java.doc.60_26/vm626/J9/VM/alloc_large_page.html


1M nonpageable

        This page size applies to object heap large pages. The JIT code cache cannot be allocated in 1M nonpageable large pages.
        This page size is supported only on the 64-bit SDK for z/OS, not the 31-bit SDK.
        This page size requires z/OS V1.10 with APAR OA25485, and a System z10® processor or later.
        A system programmer must configure z/OS for 1M nonpageable large pages.
        Users who require large pages must be authorized to the IARRSM.LRGPAGES resource in the RACF (or an equivalent security product) FACILITY class with read authority.
